.\docs\transparency.md:55:The Vexxhost host (Canadian-owned hosting, MontrÃ©al) runs `scripts/egress_lockdown.sh` which installs iptables rules in BOTH `OUTPUT` (host-originated) and `DOCKER-USER` (container-forwarded) chains. Off-allowlist traffic on 80/443 is **dropped + logged via the kernel iptables LOG target** with prefix `[POLARIS-EGRESS-DROP]`. The script's own install/config events go to `/var/log/polaris-egress.log`; the drop log lines land wherever rsyslog/journald is configured to forward kernel facility messages (typically `/var/log/kern.log` or `journalctl -k`).
.\docs\transparency.md:72:The rationale for accepting the exception: POLARIS's sovereignty constraint protects the **LLM inference path and the generated report data** â€” those run on Canadian/non-US infrastructure (Vexxhost orchestrator + OVH H200 inference). A web-search query is a short keyword string carrying no confidential research content; the sensitive artifact is the synthesized report, which never transits Serper.   45: ## §1 — Deploy day-1 (T-7 before demo, original Vexxhost path) — **PRESERVED FOR REFERENCE — NOT THE ACTIVE PATH**
  46: 
  47: > **The live demo deploys on OVH BHS5 Québec** (`polaris-orchestrator` 51.79.90.35), not Vexxhost. The Vexxhost flow below is preserved for archaeology + as a fallback if OVH BHS5 capacity changes. **Live deploy steps are in I-A-01 (#606) + `state/restart_instructions.md`.** Downstream sections (§2 smoke, §4 live demo, §8 teardown, §9 laptop fallback) inherit this preservation framing — full per-section rewrite to the current OVH flow is the "final accuracy refresh" deferred to **I-D-05 / #651** per #635 acceptance.
  48: 
  49: **Prereqs done in §0 (original Vexxhost path):** Vexxhost VM provisioned, DNS A record pointing at it, GPG keys generated, Serper API key obtained, OVH H200 server delivered + private network peered, `.env` filled, `static_accounts.yaml` filled.
  50: 
  51: ```bash
  52: # 0. Resolve the commit to pin LOCALLY (Codex iter-1 P2-3: $(git rev-parse polaris)
  53: #    inside the ssh heredoc would expand on the remote host, where the repo
  54: #    may not exist or may point at a different commit).
  55: POLARIS_REPO_COMMIT=$(git rev-parse polaris)
  56: POLARIS_DOMAIN=polaris.<your-domain>
  57: POLARIS_ACME_EMAIL=ops@<your-domain>
  58: 
  59: # 1. Stage files on the Vexxhost VM.
  60: scp infra/vexxhost/.env.example       root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN}:/root/.env  # edit FIRST
  61: scp outputs/polaris_demo_pubkey.asc   root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN}:/root/
  62: scp ~/polaris_demo_secret.asc         root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN}:/root/
  63: # I-cd-014: NEVER stage static_accounts.yaml inside the repo `config/` — it
  64: # is gitignored AND dockerignored. Operator generates it locally OUTSIDE
  65: # the repo (e.g., /tmp/polaris_secrets/static_accounts.yaml) and scps to
  66: # /root/ on the VM; `infra/vexxhost/provision.sh:102-107` then copies it
  67: # to /etc/polaris/static_accounts.yaml with chmod 640.
  68: scp /tmp/polaris_secrets/static_accounts.yaml root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN}:/root/static_accounts.yaml
  69: scp infra/vexxhost/provision.sh       root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN}:/root/
  70: 
  71: # 2. Run provisioning — pass the locally-resolved commit through ssh env.
  72: ssh root@${POLARIS_DOMAIN} \
  73:     "POLARIS_REPO_COMMIT=${POLARIS_REPO_COMMIT} \
  74:      POLARIS_DOMAIN=${POLARIS_DOMAIN} \
  75:      POLARIS_ACME_EMAIL=${POLARIS_ACME_EMAIL} \
  76:      bash /root/provision.sh"
  77: ```
  78: 
  79: Provisioning takes ~10 minutes (apt + docker pull + Next.js build + Caddy ACME). Verify:

  85: 
  86: ### §1b — Install egress lockdown + runtime tighten (mandatory before §2 smoke test)
  87: 
  88: Per Codex iter-1 P1-2 + iter-2 P2-2 + iter-3 P2: `provision.sh` does NOT auto-run egress lockdown (first compose build needs pypi/npmjs/debian access). After the first `docker compose up -d` succeeds, SSH into the host and run BOTH:
  89: 
  90: ```bash
  91: ssh root@polaris.<your-domain>
  92: # Inside the SSH session:
  93: 
  94: # 1. Install IPv4 + IPv6 lockdown with the FULL allowlist (build-time hosts
  95: #    still included so re-runs of `docker compose build` work).
  96: sudo bash /opt/polaris/scripts/egress_lockdown.sh
  97: 
  98: # 2. Tighten by stripping the build-time block (GitHub, Docker registry,
  99: #    Cloudflare CDN, pypi, npmjs, debian, cloudsmith) from the runtime
 100: #    allowlist. After this step `/transparency` reports
 101: #    build_time_hosts_pruned: true.
 102: sudo bash /opt/polaris/scripts/egress_runtime_tighten.sh
 103: 
 104: # 3. Verify all 4 chains.
 105: sudo iptables -L POLARIS_EGRESS_HOST -n -v | head -20
 106: sudo iptables -L POLARIS_EGRESS_DOCKER -n -v | head -20
 107: sudo ip6tables -L POLARIS_EGRESS_HOST_V6 -n -v | head -20
 108: sudo ip6tables -L POLARIS_EGRESS_DOCKER_V6 -n -v | head -20
 109: 
 110: # 4. Confirm the pruned flag is visible to /transparency.
 111: curl -fsS https://polaris.<your-domain>/transparency | jq '.build_time_hosts_pruned'
 112: # expected: true
 113: ```
 114: 
 115: All four chains (iptables + ip6tables × OUTPUT + DOCKER-USER) must show DROP rules at the bottom + the allowlisted IPs as ACCEPT. Without these two steps the deploy claims egress controls but they are NOT enforced — `/transparency`'s `enforcement_layer` field would be inaccurate AND `build_time_hosts_pruned` would remain false, indicating that GitHub/Docker/pypi/npm are still reachable from the runtime.

 117: ## §2 — Smoke test (T-3 before demo)
 118: 
 119: Authenticate, submit a clinical question, verify the bundle round-trips:
 120: 
 121: ```bash
 122: TOKEN=$(curl -fsS -X POST https://polaris.<your-domain>/api/v6/auth/login \
 123:     -H 'content-type: application/json' \
 124:     -d '{"username":"carney_office","password":"<reviewer-pw>"}' \
 125:     | jq -r .access_token)
 126: 
 127: # Submit a run.
 128: RUN_ID=$(curl -fsS -X POST https://polaris.<your-domain>/api/v6/runs \
 129:     -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
 130:     -H 'content-type: application/json' \
 131:     -d '{"template":"clinical","question":"Is tirzepatide effective for type 2 diabetes?"}' \
 132:     | jq -r .run_id)
 133: echo "Run: $RUN_ID"
 134: 
 135: # Tail the event stream.
 136: curl -N -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
 137:     https://polaris.<your-domain>/api/v6/stream/$RUN_ID
 138: 
 139: # Fetch the signed bundle.
 140: curl -fsS -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
 141:     -o bundle.tar.gz \
 142:     https://polaris.<your-domain>/api/v6/runs/$RUN_ID/bundle.tar.gz
 143: tar -xzf bundle.tar.gz
 144: 
 145: # Verify the GPG signature from the operator workstation (NOT from inside
 146: # the deploy — the whole point is independent verification).
 147: cd audit_*/
 148: curl -fsS https://polaris.<your-domain>/transparency/pubkey.asc | gpg --import
 149: gpg --verify manifest.yaml.asc manifest.yaml
 150: ```
 151: 
 152: Expect: `Good signature from "POLARIS Carney Demo <signing@polaris.local>"`.

 180: ## §5 — Fallback laptop (sovereign — no US KMS dependency)
 181: 
 182: If the Vexxhost deploy is unreachable (DNS, network outage, etc.) during the demo:
 183: 
 184: **One-time setup (T-3 before demo):** populate the laptop's `.env` + `/etc/polaris/static_accounts.yaml` from an encrypted offline secret bundle. No US-owned KMS (AWS Secrets Manager / GCP KMS / Azure Key Vault) is on the sovereign hot-path; the operator workstation holds the master `polaris_demo_secrets.tar.gz.gpg`, decrypted by the operator's personal GPG key (NOT the demo signing key — different keyring).
 185: 
 186: ```bash
 187: cd /local/polaris
 188: 
 189: # 1. Decrypt the offline secret bundle (operator's personal GPG key).
 190: gpg --decrypt ~/polaris_demo_secrets.tar.gz.gpg | tar -xz -C /tmp/polaris_secrets
 191: # Bundle layout (encrypt-only-once, kept on a YubiKey + paper backup):
 192: #   /tmp/polaris_secrets/.env                  — same as infra/vexxhost/.env.example, filled in
 193: #   /tmp/polaris_secrets/static_accounts.yaml  — bcrypt-hashed reviewer pwd
 194: #   /tmp/polaris_secrets/gpg_private_key.asc   — POLARIS demo signing key (private)
 195: 
 196: # 2. Stage .env at repo root (compose reads this).
 197: cp /tmp/polaris_secrets/.env .env
 198: chmod 600 .env
 199: 
 200: # 3. Stage static_accounts.yaml at /etc/polaris (matches Vexxhost host path).
 201: sudo mkdir -p /etc/polaris
 202: sudo chmod 750 /etc/polaris
 203: sudo cp /tmp/polaris_secrets/static_accounts.yaml /etc/polaris/static_accounts.yaml
 204: sudo chmod 640 /etc/polaris/static_accounts.yaml
 205: 
 206: # 4. Import the GPG private key into a separate laptop keyring.
 207: mkdir -p ~/.gnupg-polaris && chmod 700 ~/.gnupg-polaris
 208: gpg --homedir ~/.gnupg-polaris --batch --import /tmp/polaris_secrets/gpg_private_key.asc
 209: 
 210: # 5. Shred the decrypted plaintext.
 211: shred -u /tmp/polaris_secrets/.env /tmp/polaris_secrets/gpg_private_key.asc
 212: shred -u /tmp/polaris_secrets/static_accounts.yaml
 213: rmdir /tmp/polaris_secrets
 214: 
 215: # 6. Bring up the stack.
 216: docker compose -f docker-compose.v6.yml down
 217: docker compose -f docker-compose.v6.yml up -d --build
 218: 
 219: # 7. Smoke test.
 220: curl -fsS http://localhost:8000/health
 221: curl -fsS http://localhost:8000/transparency | jq
 222: ```
 223: 
 224: Localhost demo at http://localhost:3000. Auth + signing + sovereignty filter all behave identically to the Vexxhost deploy since the laptop loads the SAME secrets. `/transparency` will show `provider: "fallback_laptop"` instead of `provider: "vexxhost"` — disclose this if a reviewer asks why.
 225: 
 226: **Fallback LLM backend:** the laptop cannot reach OVH H200's private IP. Set `POLARIS_LLM_BACKEND=openrouter` in the laptop `.env` and document this in the demo narration: "Vexxhost down → OpenRouter (US) used as transitional fallback for inference; the sovereign deploy path uses self-hosted vLLM."

 275: ## §9 — Known limitations (disclose during demo if asked)
 276: 
 277: - Single-VM Vexxhost (no HA pair) — for demo window only
 278: - Manual GPG private key rotation (auto-rotation via Vexxhost Hashicorp Vault is Phase-2)
 279: - Pipeline-A only (pipeline-B legacy + pipeline-C frozen per architecture.md §5)
 280: - ~20-domain egress allowlist enforced via iptables on the VM (no managed cloud NACL on Vexxhost compute path — sovereign tradeoff vs hyperscaler defense-in-depth)
 281: - /docs + /redoc + /openapi.json public for operator ergonomics — gate to admin in Phase-2
 282: - TLS certs from Let's Encrypt (Internet Security Research Group, US 501(c)(3)). The cert is a public attestation; no data leaves to ISRG. Sovereign-strict tradeoff: replacing with a Canadian CA is Phase-2.
